CONFIDENTIAL AND INADMISSIBLE OFFER OF COMPROMISE PURSUANT TO KENTUCKY RULE OF EVIDENCE 408

VIA EMAIL: [EMAIL-3] Allstate Insurance Company

Re: Our Client: Caryn McCay Your Insured: Caryn McCay Date of Incident: July 30, 2023 Claim No.: [PHONE-1224]

Dear All Insurance Company Decision-Makers:

The following is a settlement demand on behalf of our client, Caryn McCay (“Ms. McCay” or “our client”), for the injuries she sustained on July 30, 2023, when Ms. McCay was injured a collision involving Bradley Keene (“Mr. Keene” or “your insured”).

This demand is prepared in an attempt to resolve our client’s claim and is a privileged settlement communication under K.R.E. 408. This demand is not intended for use in future litigation without our consent. No information contained herein should be considered a factual or legal admission by our client.

We expect that you will provide us with a list of any additional items you need to fully evaluate this demand within 15 days of the date of this letter. We will respond to any requests you make for additional information forthwith. We also ask that this demand be immediately forwarded to all insurance company decision-makers and, of course, the insured policyholder.




1. FACTS & LIABILITY

On July 30, 2023, Ms. McCay was the driver of a vehicle traveling westbound on Man o’ War Boulevard in Lexington, Fayette County, Kentucky. At the same time, Mr. Keene was the driver of a vehicle traveling eastbound on Man o’ War Boulevard. Ms. McCay approached and lawfully proceeded through the intersection of Crosby Drive when, suddenly and without warning, Mr. Keene attempted an unlawful left turn, entered Ms. McCay’s lane of travel, and caused her vehicle to collide with the front passenger side of Mr. Keene’s vehicle. Upon impact, the airbags of Ms. McCay’s vehicle were immediately deployed, and she hit both her knees against the dashboard and struck the front of her head against the dashboard, the window, and the steering wheel as she was jolted violently within the interior of the vehicle, which was propelled into an adjacent brick wall before finally coming to rest. The collision resulted in Ms. McCay sustaining significant personal injuries and other damages.

As exposed in the Kentucky Uniform Police Traffic Collision Report,! Officer Samuel Price of the Lexington Police Department investigated the collision and determined that Mr. Keene was the sole party responsible for the collision due to his improper turning.

The conditions for establishing liability, in this case, are clear. Mr. Keene owed a duty of care to the other drivers on the road. Pursuant to KY Rev Stat § 189.330(9): “The operator of a vehicle

intending to turn to the left within an intersection or into an alley, private road, or driveway shall yield the right-of-way to any vehicle approaching from the opposite direction which is within the intersection or so close thereto as to constitute an immediate hazard.” On the date of loss, Mr. Keene lacked attentiveness, failed to yield the right of way when turning left, lacked all due care, and caused a collision with Ms. McCay’s vehicle. As a result of Mr. Keene’s acts and/or omissions on July 30, 2023, Ms. McCay suffered significant personal injuries and damages for which Mr. Keene is undoubtedly liable.

Summary e On July 30, 2023, EMS was dispatched to the scene of the collision. Upon arrival, EMS personnel found Ms. McCay sitting in the driver’s seat of her vehicle. Ms. McCay complained of pain in her head, neck, left arm, and left knee After an emergent medical examination, EMS personnel determined that Ms. McCay required additional treatment and care, at which time they administered a cervical collar and transported her to UK Hospital.

Summary e On July 30, 2023, Ms. McCay arrived at the emergency room via ambulance for emergent treatment and care. Upon arrival, Ms. McCay complained of pain in her neck, chest, and middle back. The attending emergency physician ordered X-rays of Ms. McCay’s chest and pelvis, CT angiograms of her head, neck, chest, abdomen, and pelvis, and CT scans of her head, face, cervical spine, thoracic spine, lumbar spine, and bony pelvis, which revealed no acute abnormalities. After a clinical examination and reviewing the results of her diagnostic




imaging, the attending emergency physician discharged Ms. McCay with instructions to take Ibuprofen and Tylenol as needed and follow up with her primary care physician.

3.4. Loss of Household Services

As a result of the July 30, 2023, incident, we estimate that Ms. McCay has been and will continue to be unable to contribute $9,002.99 in labor in the form of past and future household services. Our calculation rests on three variables:

1. Before her incident, we assume that Ms. McCay contributed an average of 2.11 hours of household chores per day to the household, in line with the average contribution of persons of similar age and gender in America.

2. We assume that the monetary value of Ms. McCay’s labor is consistent with the average housekeeping salary of $12.68 an hour in the Commonwealth of Kentucky, as estimated from the May 2022 report on Occupational Employment and Wages by the U.S. Bureau of Labor Statistics.

3. In our estimation, Ms. McCay suffered a 100% impairment from contributing to household chores from July 30, 2023, to March 12, 2024, and a conservative 10% impairment for three years thereafter.

Assuming no further impairment of household chores after March 12, 2027, solely for simplicity and convenience of early settlement, we calculate the value of Ms. McCay’s loss of household services between July 30, 2023, and March 12, 2027, at $9,002.99.

Loss of Household Services Schedule

Start of End of Loss Hours Per

Loss Date Date Hourly Rate Day Impairment Net Loss 7/30/2023 3/12/2024 $12.68 2.11 100% $6,073.34 3/13/2024 3/12/2027 $12.68 2.11 10% $2,929.65

Total Loss of Household Services $9,002.99

The value of lost household services, which includes losses for tasks the injured claimant provided around the home, are cognizable damages in personal injury cases in Kentucky where proof of such loss is substantiated by a preponderance of the evidence. Primal Vantage Co., Inc. v. O’Bryan, No. 2018-CA-0000106-MR, 2019 WL 6044870, at *2 (Ky. Ct. App. Nov. 15, 2019), aff'd in part, rev'd in part and remanded, No. 2020-SC-0247-DG, 2022 WL 3641122 (Ky. Aug. 18, 2022). Recovery for the loss of household services should be limited to the period of recuperation, and, if there is a permanent impairment of a person’s ability to perform household tasks, that item of damage would be included within the claim for the permanent impairment of earning capacity. Schulz v. Chadwell, 558 S.W.2d 183, 189 (Ky. Ct. App. 1977).

12




3.5. Past and Future Pain and Suffering

There is no question that the July 30, 2023, incident caused Ms. McCay a great deal of physical and emotional pain and suffering. As a result of the incident, Ms. McCay suffered serious injuries that affected, and continue to affect, her quality of life.

Ms. McCay’s pain was aggravated by simple self-care tasks that she must perform daily, such as bathing or putting on her shoes and socks, forcing her to relive the collision with each jolt of pain. In fact, Ms. McCay has found that she must exercise a great deal of caution in her approach to virtually any physical or daily activity. Even in moments of solitude, there is truly never a moment in which she is not reminded of the collision.

Furthermore, Ms. McCay experiences challenges in getting a restful night’s sleep as she is unable to remain in one position for long without pain and discomfort. This lack of quality sleep has had a profound impact on her overall well-being and ability to function during the day. It affects her energy levels, concentration, and mood, which makes it difficult for her to engage in daily activities and maintain a normal routine.

Additionally, the trauma of the ordeal and the severity of its aftermath has left Ms. McCay with residual anxiety, accompanying the tangible effects of her injuries with an experience of persistent emotional distress.

As a result of her pain, fatigue, and emotional distress, Ms. McCay struggles to complete simple household chores that she used to be able to complete with ease prior to the subject collision. As she is unable to lift heavy objects, taking out the trash and shopping for groceries has become immensely challenging, upending her sense of normalcy as she endeavored to move forward with her life.

Professionally, Ms. McCay’s pain and limitations made it difficult for her to perform her job effectively. Nevertheless, after initially missing work, Ms. McCay was forced to endure such pain in order to preserve her stream of income and her very livelihood, as she continued to work in spite of her injuries even when she had not yet fully recovered.

Ms. McCay has ultimately been forced to take a passive role in her own life as she focuses on her recovery. She is unable to participate socially as she could before the collision, depriving her of the opportunity to connect with her peers at a time when their support could most reassure her.

Even independently, activities that Ms. McCay had previously enjoyed now only serve to

aggravate her discomfort, isolating her within the confines of her pain and allowing it to define the expansiveness of her life.

13




Because of your insured’s negligence, Ms. McCay has been forced to assimilate to the new reality imposed by her injuries and is facing the prospect of years of treatment to achieve the relief she deserves. Ms. McCay can no longer simply go about her normal day without constant reminders of everything that this collision has taken away from her. She only hopes to regain a semblance of the life she once knew and looks forward to the opportunity to heal, both physically and emotionally.

All this considered, Ms. McCay’s pain and suffering, physical impairment, and mental anguish as a result of the July 30, 2023, collision has had an undeniable impact on her past, present, and future quality of life, and this should remain at the forefront of your consideration as you evaluate her significant noneconomic damages.

The goal of compensatory damages is to make the injured party whole to the extent it is possible to measure the injury in terms of money. Ky. Cent. Ins. Co. v. Schneider, 15 S.W.3d 373, 374 (Ky. 2000). Damages should include fair compensation for any physical or mental suffering caused by the injury. Ky. Cent. Ins. Co. v. Schneider, 15 S.W.3d 373, 374 (Ky. 1995). There is no set rule for computing damages for pain and suffering. The general rule is that the damages must be reasonable, free from sentiment and free from punishment so as not to amount to punitive damages. Noel v. Creary, 385 S.W.2d 951, 953 (Ky. 1965). The probability of future pain and suffering may be considered when calculating damages if the evidence shows that future pain and suffering may stem from the injury. Nussbaum v. Caskey, 235 Ky. 640, 32 S.W.2d 18, 19 (Ky. App. 1930).

Liability is clear. Should this case go to a jury, the sole question to answer would be how much money Ms. McCay is entitled to receive under Kentucky law.

Verdict Analysis

Based on case results with similar facts, we assert that Ms. McCay is entitled to, at least, past and future pain and suffering damages in the amount of $275,000.00. As justification for this claim, we direct your attention to the following:

McHugh y. State Farm

Citation 2018 KY Trial Ct. Rev. Lexis 56 Jurisdiction Jefferson County, Kentucky

Award $285,000.00 (The entire amount awarded in non-economic damages)

14




Case Facts Eric McHugh, a Louisville police officer, was involved in a right-of-way crash on March 25, 2014. It occurred on Eastern Parkway near the University of Louisville. The tortfeasor, Michael Robinson, turned left in front of McHugh. McHugh was operating an unmarked vehicle. It was a serious crash with visible and dramatic property damage.

McHugh first moved against Robinson, a State Farm insured, and entered a settlement. The amount of the settlement is not known. McHugh then sought UIM benefits against his insurer, also State Farm.

This case was tried for two days. The jury in this case considered pain and suffering damages only. McHugh took $285,000.00 for that category.

Injuries McHugh was taken to the ER where he was treated and released for soft-tissue injuries. He subsequently followed up with six physical therapy treatments for neck pain. Beyond his neck pain, McHugh has also reported knee pain. McHugh saw a neurologist twice for knee pain. On both visits, the neurologist identified a bruised knee. Despite the simple bruise, McHugh has continued to report knee pain. It was 4 1/2 years from the date of McHugh’s last treatment to the jury trial. Plaintiff's IME confirmed the knee injury.

In each instance, the plaintiff above and Ms. McCay suffered painful and significant personal injuries and damages as a result of the reckless, careless, or otherwise negligent conduct of a liable tortfeasor. Therefore, we find that this verdict represents a strong benchmark for estimating the minimum amount of compensation a similarly situated jury would award Ms. McCay today.

Per Diem Analysis

Our conservative per diem analysis shows that Ms. McCay’s claim for past, present, and future pain and suffering is valued at $276,448.00. A jury will consider not only Ms. McCay’s initial pain and suffering to date, but also her subsequent pain and suffering. Below are some very conservative figures we would present to a jury to consider, in addition to her other damages:

e@ $28.00/hr. for initial pain and suffering from July 30, 2023, to March 12, 2024; and

e@ $10.00/hr. for subsequent pain and suffering from March 12, 2024, to March 12, 2027.

Pain & Suffering

Initial Pain & Suffering

15




Initial Period (in Days) 226

Waking Hours/Day 16.0 Reasonable Compensation/Hour $28.00 Total Initial Pain & Suffering $101,248.00 Subsequent Pain & Suffering Subsequent Years with Pain 3 Waking Hours/Day 16.0 Reasonable Compensation/Hour $10.00 Total Subsequent Pain & Suffering $175,200.00

Total Pain and Suffering $276,448.00

In light of the per diem analysis above, we assert that $275,000.00 is fair and equitable compensation for Ms. McCay’s initial and subsequent pain and suffering.

4. DEMAND TO SETTLE We believe that the above evaluation is a fair and reasonable calculation of our client’s damages.

As you will note, our client’s economic and non-economic damages total at least $369,248.34. Our client will settle her claim for a minimum of the policy limits.

If a software product is being used to generate payout ranges as to this claim, we request that you communicate the range of results generated by your software. Please respond within 15 days of receipt of this demand. If the terms of this demand are not accepted, we have been authorized by our client to promptly file suit. Please feel free to contact me should you have any questions.

KENTUCKY UNIFORM POLICE TRAFFIC COLLISION REPORT - NARRATIVE 9000 [MASTER FILE# 72928252

INVESTIGATING AGENCY LEXINGTON POLICE DEPARTMENT AGENCY ORI 0340200 LOCAL CODE [PHONE-11]

On [DOB-1216] at 2144 hours | responded to the intersection of Man O War Boulevard and Crosby Drive in reference to a dispatched vehicle collision with injuries. When | arrived on scene | made contact with both involved units and their operators.

| observed that Unit 1 (F2M081) appeared to have been initially struck on the front passenger side, and

had then collided with a fixed electrical box beside the traffic signal support pole, destroying it. The operator of Unit 1 appeared to have suffered an injury to his head, and had been pushed from the driver's seat to the front passenger seat during the collision. The operator of Unit 1 was unable to provide a coherent statement in reference to the collision. He stated that the last thing he remembered was driving down Clays Mill Road.

The operator of Unit 2 stated that she had been driving on the inner loop of Man O War Blvd. approaching the intersection with Crosby Drive. She stated that she proceeded through the intersection, and Unit 1 made a left hand turn from the outer loop of Man O War, into the intersection. She stated Unit 1 pulled out in front of her too quickly for her to stop.

Both the operators were transported to UK Hospital by Lexington Fire Department ambulance. Both vehicles sustained severe damage. Both vehicles were towed by Robert's Towing to their lot.

BWC Present - Activated - Not Reviewed Ofc. S. Price 57494

Narrative

EC14 dispatched for vehicle collision at above location. EC11 found law enforcement, E21, and EC1 on scene. £21 gave vitals and assessment. Patient was sitting in drivers seat and alert to crew arrival. Patient complaint of left arm pain, left knee pain, neck pain and head pain. Patient advised she was traveling about 45 mph and was unrestrained. Air bag deployed. Spidering on front windshield was noted by crew. Patient was placed in C collar. Crew used long board to moved patient from vehicle. Patient denied loss of consciousness. Patient was fully immobilized by crew. Patient was secured to stretcher and moved to ambulance without incident. Vitals taken, IV established, 4 lead showed sinus. Exam found small lacerations to left forearm and pain on palpation

to left:knee. Patient requested transport to UKMC and was transported with advance notification given to hospital. During transport patient was given suppottive care and monitored with no new complaints or changes. Report given and care transferred to ED nursing staff. EC11 available.

HPI

Chief Complaint Patient presents with ¢ Motor Vehicle Crash

Room/Bed: 72/72 History of Present Illness

History provided by: Patient Language interpreter used: No

Caryn Leigh McCay is a 50 y.o. female with PMH of diabetes who presents to the emergency department from scene for evaluation as a trauma due to a MVC. Patient was a(n) restrained driver without ejection. She reports driving at approximately 45 miles per hour when another car pulled out in front of her, causing her to hit a brick wall. FINDINGS:

CT Head without:

CT scan of face: Subtle irregularity the nasal bones correlate clinically for tenderness.

CTA Head: There is normal vascular anatomy. There is no evidence of vascular injury, specifically no arterial stenosis, occlusion, dissection, or pseudoaneurysm. The intracranial venous structures are also fairly well opacified and appear unremarkable.

CTA Neck: There is normal vascular anatomy. There is no evidence of vascular injury, specifically no arterial stenosis, occlusion, dissection, or pseudoaneurysm. There is 0% stenosis of the ICA origins by NASCET criteria.

Degenerative changes in spine.

Impression: 1. No acute intracranial abnormality.

2. Normal CTA of the head and neck without evidence of vascular injury. 3. No definite facial fractures. See above

Resulting lab: IMAGING

Narrative:

CLINICAL INDICATION:

poly trauma

TECHNIQUE:

Imaging of the chest abdomen and pelvis was performed, from thoracic inlet through pubic symphysis, using spiral technique, following administration of IV contrast, Omnipaque 350, 100 mL according to the CTA thoracic aorta/chest and CTA Abdomen/Pelvis protocol. Reformatted images in the coronal, sagittal, and oblique planes were generated from the axial data set to facilitate diagnostic accuracy. In addition, 3D images were created and reviewed.

Multiple axial CT images were obtained through level of pelvis per CT Bony Pelvis protocol. The axial CT data set was used to

generate high resolution reformatted images in the coronal and sagittal planes to facilitate diagnostic accuracy and treatment planning.

Total DLP (Dose-Length Product): 4958 mGy-cm. Please note: The reported value represents the total of one or more individual components during the CT acquisition on this date and at this time, and as such, the same value may appear in more than one CT report depending on the interpreting/reporting physicians.

COMPARISON: CTA chest abdomen pelvis 4/16/2016

FINDINGS: Chest:

Lower neck: The supraglottic soft tissues appear circumferentially thickened.

Aorta/Vessels: No acute thoracic aortic pathology. No periaortic hematoma. No filling defect within the pulmonary arteries to suggest pulmonary embolism.

Pleural/Pericardial Space: No pneumothorax. No pleural effusions. No pericardial effusion.

Printed on 10/11/23 9:33 AM Page 153

Bones: No acute fracture within the chest. Sclerotic changes and cortical destruction of the left posterior ribs 3 through 8, new from 2016.

Abdomen: Vessels: The abdominal aorta and its major branches are unremarkable.

Liver/Gallbladder/Biliary System: The liver demonstrates homogeneous enhancement. Cholecystectomy No intra- or extra- hepatic biliary ductal dilatation.

Spleen: The spleen enhances homogeneously.

Pancreas: The pancreas enhances homogeneously.

Adrenals: The adrenals are morphologically unremarkable.

Kidneys: The kidneys demonstrate symmetric nephrogram and excretion. No renal or ureteral calculi. No hydronephrosis.

Bowel/Mesentery: The small bowel loops are not dilated. The large bowel loops are not dilated. The appendix is visualized and normal.

Lymph Nodes: No lymphadenopathy within the abdomen or pelvis. Fluid Survey: No free fluid in the abdomen. No free fluid in the pelvis. Pelvis: The pelvic viscera are unremarkable.

CT bony pelvis no pelvic fracture.

2. No acute findings in the chest, abdomen, or pelvis.

AUTHORIZATIONS & AGREEMENTS

Patient Labe! Here)

A mother living with HIV can pass HIV to her baby, but this is now very uncommon in the US as long as the mother knows that she has HIV and is being treated. It is also very rare that HIV is passed by blood transfusions or transplanted organs, because all donated blood and organs are now tested for HIV.

Hi¥ is mostly spread by people who do not know they have HIV. This is why it is so important ta get lested for HIV at least once in yaur lifetime, and at least every 6 months if you are having sex without candorns or sharing needles.

Treatment with Controilted Substances

Federal and state laws regulate controlied substances (drugs) that may be abused. Kentucky law requires that you conseni to treatment with these drugs before you can receive them. Some illnesses and injuries can result in pain. Some drugs can make the paln more tolerable. Some other drugs can increase focus and reduce hyperactivity. Use of these drugs can cause nausea, sleepiness, drowsiness, vomiting, constipation, sleeplessness, loss of appetite, agitatian, aggravation of depression, dry mouth, confusion, slawer breathing, and loss of coordination making il unsafe to drive or operate machinery. These drugs can result in physical dependence, meaning that abrupt stopping may lead to withdrawal symptoms, psychological dependence, meaning that stopping may cause you to crave the drug, tolerance, meaning you need more drugs ta get the same effect and addiction, meaning you may develop problems based on genetic or other factors. You must tell your doctor if you are pregnant or are considering pregnancy.

Living Wills

Please tell your provider if yau have a Living Will, Advance Directive, Power of Attorney or any other document that allows someone to make healthcare decisions for you or documents your wishes regarding your care. What everyone needs to know about AIDS

Kentucky law requires that we intorm you about AIDS.

HIV stands for "human immunodeficiency virus," which is a virus that attacks the body's immune system, HI makes it harder for people with it to recover from other infections and Illnesses. AIDS stands for "acquired immune deficiency syndrome," which is the health effects that happen if HIV is not treated. With treatment, a person living with HIV can be healthy and live nearly as long as a person who does not have HIV. Treatment for HIV also greatly lowers the chance that someone with HIV will pass it to others.

HIV is not spread through activities such as hugging or shaking hands or sharing a drinking glass. HIV is only spread through blood, sexual fluids or breast milk.

This usually happens by: * Having sex without condoms * Sharing needles

Additional Information

Preventing Falls in the Home

As you get older, falls are more likely. That's because your reaction time slows. Your muscles and joints may also get stiffer, making them less flexible. Illness, medications, and vision changes can also affect your balance. A fall could leave you unable to live on your own. To make your home safer, follow these tips:

Moving:

* Get up slowly after you sit or lie down. + Wear shoes inside and outside the house, Do not go barefoot or wear slippers. Floors:

.

Put nonskid pads under area rugs.

Remove throw rugs. Or hold the rugs in place with 2-sided tape or nonslip backing.

Replace worn floor coverings.

Tack carpets firmly to each step on carpeted stairs. Put nonskid strips on the edges of uncarpeted stairs. Keep floors and stairs free of clutter and cords.

Arrange furniture so there are clear pathways.

Clean up any spills right away.

Stairs:

+ Always use the handrails. There should be handrails on both sides. The handrails should be as long as the stairs. + Use a contrasting color on the top edge of all steps. This will help you see the steps better.

Why do | need a naloxone prescription?

Naloxone is a rescue medicine, It is only used to treat an opioid overdose. Most people who are prescribed an opioid do not have any problems. But even if you are careful, there is still a risk of accidental overdose.

Make sure someone close to you knows the signs of overdose and how to give naloxone.

Most opioid deaths are accidents

Opioid overdose deaths are happening more often in the U.S. In fact, a person dies from opioid overdose every 11 minutes,

+ In 2017, opioid overdose caused more than 47,000 deaths. + Most of those deaths were accidents. + Nearly 4 out of 10 people who die from opioid overdose have an opioid prescription.

Death from overdose is more common than you think.

Attached Information MVA, No Sertousdnjury (English)

Motor Vehicle Accident: No Serious Injury

You or your child have been seen today because of a car accident. Your exam does not show any sign of serious injury from your car accident. It's important to watch for any new symptoms that might be a sign of hidden injury.

\t can be normal to feel sore and tight in your muscles and back the next day, and not just the muscles you initially injured. Remember, all the parts of your body are connected, so while initially one area hurts, the next day another may hurt. Injuries cause inflammation, which then causes the muscles to tighten up and hurt more. After the initial worsening, it should slowly improve over the next few days. However, report more severe pain to your healthcare provider.

Even without a definite head injury, you can still get a concussion from your head suddenly jerking forward, backward, or sideways. It's common to have a mild headache and feel tired, nauseated, or dizzy. Concussions and even bleeding can still occur, especially if you've had a recent injury, take blood thinners, or are over age 65, Know the warning signs that you should report to your healthcare provider.

Even without physical injury, a car accident can be very stressful. It can cause emotional or mental symptoms after the event. These may include:

* General sense of anxiety and fear

* Recurring thoughts or nightmares about the accident

* Trouble sleeping or changes in appetite

* Feeling depressed, sad, or low in energy

* Being irritable or easily upset

+ Feeling the need to avoid activities, places, or people that remind you of the accident |n most cases, these are normal reactions. And they're not severe enough to interfere with your normal activities. They should go away in a few days or a few weeks. Talk with your healthcare provider if these reactions last longer, get worse, or disrupt your daily life.

Home care Muscle pain, sprains and strains

Even if you have no visible injury, it's common to be sore all over, and have new aches and pains the first couple of days after an accident. Take it easy at first, and don't overdo it.

* At first, don't try to stretch out the sore spots. If there is a strain, stretching may make it worse.

* You can use an ice pack or cold compress on the sore spots for up to 20 minutes at a time, as often as you feel comfortable. This may help reduce the inflammation, swelling, and pain. To make an ice pack, put ice cubes in a plastic bag that seals at the top. Wrap the bag in a thin towel or cloth. Don't put the ice pack directly on the skin.

+ Sometimes, after the pain and inflammation heal you can be left with a good amount of stiffness. |n this case, you can use a heating pad, especially on your low back,

Wound care

* Ifyou have any scrapes or abrasions, they often heal in about10 days. It's important to keep the abrasions clean while they first start to heal, Follow wound care instructions from your healthcare provider. Watch for early signs of infection such as;

= Increasing redness, warmth, or swelling around the wound « Fever » Red streaking lines around the wound

[DOB-214] - ED in PAV A Emergency Department (continued)

» Draining pus Medicines

* Talk to your healthcare provider before taking new medicine, especially if you have other medical problems or are taking other medicines.

If you need anything for pain, you can take acetaminophen or ibuprofen, unless you were given a different pain medicine to use. Ibuprofen is an anti-inflammatory agent and helps more with muscle soreness. Talk with your provider before using these medicines if you have medicine allergies, chronic liver or kidney disease, stomach ulcer or gastraintestinal bleeding, or are taking blood thinner medicines, Always follow your provider's instructions.

Be careful if you're given prescription pain medicines, narcotics, or medicines for muscle spasm. They can make you sleepy, dizzy and can affect your coordination, reflexes and judgment. Don't drive or do work where you can injure yourself when taking them.

Follow-up care

Follow up with your healthcare provider, or as advised. If emational or mental symptoms persist or get worse, follow up with your provider right away. You may have a more serious traumatic stress reaction. There are treatments that can help.

\f X-rays or a CT scan were done, you'll be told if there is a change that affects treatment. Call 911

Call 911 if any of these occur:

* Trouble breathing

One pupil is larger than the other

Repeated vomiting

Headache that worsens and does not go away Restlessness or agitation

Confusion, drowsiness, or trouble arousing

Fainting, loss of consciousness, convulsions, or seizures Rapid heart rate

Trouble with speech or sight

Trouble walking, loss of balance, numbness or weakness in 1 side of your body, facial droop When to get medical advice

Call your healthcare provider right away if any of the following occur:

* New or worsening pain in neck, back, belly, arm, or leg

* Redness, swelling, or pus coming from any wound

* Mental and emotional symptoms that don't get better or that get worse StayWell last reviewed this educational content on 1/1/2022

She reports she has to lay down when she gets home from work and sometimes while on breaks at work due to pain. She reports pain/difficulty going up/down stairs, more difficulty going down. Can go reciprocally up with B use of hands but goes down one step at a time when descending stairs. She just moved into her son's house which is 3 stories and she has to be able to go up and down stairs all 3 levels regularly for laundry, caring for dogs. S

She was also referred to see pain specialist and chiropractor (evaluation next week). She reports she was off work almost 2 months, she is now working 2 days a week and goal is to work 5 days a week starting in 1 month. She reports she had a radiograph done on her right knee and there is a tumor in her knee, which was minimally painful before MVA.

Oswestry Disability Index

The Oswestry Disability Index is an extremely important tool that researchers and disability evaluators use to measure a patient's functional disability.

Section 1 - Pain Intensity: The pain is moderate at the moment. (2)

Section 6 - Standing: Pain prevents me from standing more than 1 hour. (2)

Section 2 - Personal Care (Washing, Dressing, etc.): | can look after myself normally but it causes extra pain. (1)

Section 7 - Sleeping: Because of pain | have less than 4 hours sleep. (3)

Section 3 - Lifting: Pain prevents me from lifting heavy weights, but | can manage light to medium weights if they are

conveniently positioned. (3)

Section 4 - Walking: Pain prevents me from walking more than 1/2 mile. (2) Section 9 - Social Life: Pain has restricted my social life to my home. (4) Section 5 - Sitting: Pain prevents me from sitting more than one hour. (2) Section 10 - Traveling: Pain restricts me to journeys of less than one hour. (3)

Total Score: 22 /50

Disability in Percent: 44 %

Interpretation: 41% to 60%: Severe disability

ASSESSMENT

Diagnosis

Summary: Pt presents to PT re-eval with objective improvements in LE strength, ROM, functional mobility, and LEFS score. Still presents with deficits in gait pattern, quad/HS strength R>L, and tissue extensibility R>L all of which impair her ability to squat, stand, walk, navigate stairs and perform repetitive tasks without increase in RLE pain and compensations. At this time pt is appropriate for con't skilled PT to address above objective and functional deficits to safely return to her PLOF.

See code details above

History of Present Condition: Pt is a 50 yo female who presents to skilled PT for evaluation with primary c/p bilateral ankle and knee pain which have been present since she was in an MVA on 7/30/23, during which she was t-boned and her knees hit the dash forcefully. She reports her pain is worse R>L. She rates her current pain a 6/10, pain at worst 10/10 in last 1-2 weeks, and pain at best 5/10 (at rest, with ice/heat, activity modification/laying down).

She reports increased pain with prolonged standing/walking (10-20 minutes), sitting (5-10 minutes), squatting, and yardwork/housework. She has difficulty getting up/down from the floor as well. She is currently working 2 days a week at the VA after 2 months off work and plans to start full-time in 4 weeks. She reports she has to lay down when she gets home from work and sometimes while on breaks at work due to pain. She reports pain/difficulty going up/down stairs, more difficulty going down. Can go reciprocally up with B use of hands but goes down one step at a time when descending stairs. She just moved into her son's house which is 3 stories and she has to be able to go up and down stairs all 3 levels regularly for laundry, caring for dogs. S

Her goal with physical therapy is to reduce symptoms in order to return to prior level of function and work full-time at the VA (working 2 days a week right now). She was also referred to see pain specialist and chiropractor (evaluation next week). She reports she was off work almost 2 months, she is now working 2 days a week and goal is to work 5 days a week starting in 1 month. She reports she had a radiograph done on her right Knee and there is a tumor in her knee, which was minimally painful before MVA.

PMH: hernia sx 2016, MVA in 2016 leading to multiple LE fractures, tumor in R knee diagnosed prior to MVA not thought to be cancerous, diabethic neuropathy, rectal cancer, DMI

Oswestry Disability Index

The Oswestry Disability Index is an extremely important tool that researchers and disability evaluators use to measure a patient's functional disability.

She has pain/difficulty with functional tasks, including prolonged standing/walking, going up/down stairs (worse going down than up), getting up/down from a chair/toilet, performing household chores, and working at the VA. Pt will benefit from skilled PT services at this time to address impairments found and return to PML of function without pain or limitation. Good prognosis and recovery with skilled PT is expected at this time.

The goal of this therapy is to increase functional capacity, improve posture, increase muscle and ligament strength to the affected body part/body region(s). Due to the complexities of the patients condition, the Dr trains and monitors Whole Body Vibration therapeutic exercises. 2 lbs. of weight was used to perform these isometric exercises. A halo posture correction device was utilized for the entirety of this therapeutic procedure. Goals noted above.

5 mm thick contiguous axial images were obtained through the abdomen and pelvis without IV contrast. Multiplanar reformats were also performed. Automated exposure control was utilized to optimize dose reduction.

Comparison [DOB-822]

Findings

The liver, spleen, adrenals, pancreas, kidneys, urinary bladder, and uterus are unremarkable.

Moderate to large amount of stool is seen throughout the colon suggesting constipation.

Appendix is normal. Urinary bladder and uterus also are unremarkable. No free fluid or pneumoperitoneum is seen. Stomach and small bowel are unremarkable. In the subcutaneous tissues of the anterior right lower abdomen there is a 1 cm nodule which probably represents a sebaceous cyst.

Impression Constipation

Otherwise no acute process

EXAMINATION: MRI of the right knee with and without contrast. SEDATION; None.

HISTORY: Anterior right knee pain x1+ years, worse in the last elght montha since MVA. Anterior swelling, numbness, weakness, popping/grinding, and stiffness with limited range of motion. Follow up mass seen on prior imaging.

COMPARISON: Comparison is made with the prior MRI from [DOB-864] and nuclear medicine study from [DOB-865].

TECHNIQUE: MRI of the right Knee with and without contrast using the 3 tesla magnet. Axial proton densily with fat saturation and T1 weighted with fat saturation, sagittal proton density and T2 welghted with fat saturation, and coronal proton density with fat saturation, T1 weighted, and oblique T2 weighted through the ACL sequences were obtained. A dose of 22 mL of Dotarem was intravenously administered, Following the injection, axial, sagittal, and coronal T1 welghted with fat saturation sequences were performed.

FINDINGS: The anterlor and posterior cruciate ligaments are Intact, There is complex tearing involving the posterior horn, posterlor root, and body of the medial meniscus. There Is moderate chondromalacla within the medlal compartment. The lateral meniscus is grossly normal in signal and morphology. The medial and lateral collateral ligamentous complexes are Intact. There Is mild-to-moderate chondromalacia within the lateral compartment with areas of full-thickness carlllage loss and a suspected Internal osteophyte tormatlon measuring 0.5 cm. The extensor mechanism is tendinopathic. There are severe arthritic changes in the palellofemoral compartment with complete

loss of artlcular cartllage seen along the lateral facet with extensive subchondral and/or osteachondral-type defects. There is osteophytosls. There Is a small suprapatellar Joint affuslon. Post contrast Images were obtalned. There are no abnormal enhancing mass lesions detected.

There Is an lrregularity with fragmentation of the lateral tiblal plateau which Is presumably a sequela of prior comminuted depressed tibial plateau fracture. There is mild cortical irregularity along the articular surface of the lateral tibial plateau. There is a very low T1 and T2 signal lesion within the lateral epiphysis and metaphysis of the lateral tibia measuring approximately 1.7 cm in mediolateral dimension x 1.9 cm in craniocaudal dimension x 1.5 cm in AP dimension.

There Is a ganglion cyst formation noted at the gastrocnemius muscle attachments, larger on the lateral attachment, measuring over 2 cm, There Is no associated enhancement.

IMPRESSION:

1. There Is posttraumatic deformity of the lateral tlblal plateau with suspected chronic comminuted fracturing. There Is persistent fragmentation. There are arthritle changes In the lateral compartment with a smail Internal ostaophyte. There Is a very low T1 and T2 signal lesion within the lateral tibia. Correlation with any prior imaging is needed if available.

A blastic lesion could potentially have a similar appearance. Radiographic correlation is needed and correlation with any more recent imaging, If avallable, There was asymmeitrle uptake within the right proximal tiblal metaphyseal reglon on the prior nuclear medicine study, which could also be related to the fracture and arthritic changes vs. ihe lesion. A photopenic defect was not visualized on the nuclear medicine study.

2. There are acivanced arthritic changes In the medial compartment with moderate chondromalacia.

AUTHORIZATION FOR RELEASE OF INFORMATION (for Use and Disclosure)

TO PATIENTS OR LEGAL DESIGNEES:

FACTS ABOUT OBTAINING YOUR MEDICAL RECORDS:

You have the right to obtain a copy of your medical records. The law requires a signed authorization formwhich contains certain criteria included on this form. This form must be fully completed before any medical information can be released. Incomplete forms may be returned for completion.

COSTS:

Kentucky law allows you one free copy of your medical record. This free copy is one requested by you for yourself or for a third party. Additional requests will cost $1.00 per page. It is advised you keep a personal copy of any medical information you request to avoid future costs of obtaining copies.

WHEN AND HOW WILL | GET MY RECORDS?

Requests will be completed within 30 days of receipt. You will be notified via mail if the records cannot be processed in 30 days. Records will be delivered as indicated on the request. If you are picking up your records, please note that they will only be held for 30 days once notice has been made that they are ready for pick-up. If they are not picked up within 30 days of the date of the notice, the copies will be destroyed and a new request will have to be completed. Please include your phone number so that we may call you when the records are ready for pick-up.

WHERE TO SEND YOUR REQUEST Mail a completed request form to one of the following addresses:

1) University of Kentucky Hospital 4) UK College of Dentistry Release of Information Section Dental Records Health Information Management Dept. 800 Rose Street D-104 Room C601 Lexington, KY 40536-0297

FACTS ABOUT OBTAINING YOUR MEDICAL RECORDS:

You have the right to obtain a copy of your medical records. The law requires a signed authorization formwhich contains certain criteria included on this form. This form must be fully completed before any medical information can be released. Incomplete forms may be returned for completion.

COSTS:

Kentucky law allows you one free copy of your medical record. This free copy is one requested by you for yourself or for a third party. Additional requests will cost $1.00 per page. It is advised you keep a personal copy of any medical information you request to avoid future costs of obtaining copies.

WHEN AND HOW WILL | GET MY RECORDS?

Requests will be completed within 30 days of receipt. You will be notified via mail if the records cannot be processed in 30 days. Records will be delivered as indicated on the request. If you are picking up your records, please note that they will only be held for 30 days once notice has been made that they are ready for pick-up. Per my electronic signature below, and pursuant to the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act (HIPAA) Privacy Regulations, 45 CFR J 64.508, the provider listed above is hereby authorized to release to The Whaley Law Firm, PSC, or a:ly of their representatives, all medical records, including but, not limited to: office nates. history, physical, consultation, notes, discharge summaries, order and progress notes, laboratory

results, nurses notes, emergency room records, operative records, in- patient records and films of x- rays, MRIs or PET scans, pharmacy and drug records, medical bills and health insurance Medicaid or Medicare records, concerning any medical teatment that I have received from you, at your institution, as well as all such records which you keep in the regular course of business that are found in my medical records file. I hereby authorize release of all records regarding mental health, psychiatric (other than psychotherapy notes which must be requested by separate authorization), chemical dependency or HIV. A photostatic copy hereof shall be as valid as the original. [ hereby authorize a free copy of my medical records pursuant to K.R.S 422.317 be sent, to the extent I have not already requested my one free copy.

The purpose of this authorization and request is to permit my attorney to obtain ALL medical information pertaining to my physical or mental condition. This authorization expires three (3} years from the date of the signature. The aforementioned expiration date has not passed, as this matter is ongoing,

I hereby authorize The Whaley Law Firm, PSC to speak to my healthcare professionals privately or to take testimony at deposition or trial as may be requested.

I have the right to revoke this authorization in writing by providing a signed, written notice of revocation to the health care provider listed above and to The Whaley Law Firm, PSC. I understand that there are exceptions to the right to revoke. Among the exceptions to the right to revoke are that an individual may not revoke an authorization to the extent that the covered entity has taken action - in reliance thereon. Medical providers may not condition treatment or payment on whether the above-listed patient executes this authorization. The information disclosed pursuant to this authorization may be subject to re-disclosure and no longer protected by the privacy regulations promulgated pursuant to the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act (HIPPA).
